# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kafka Consumer Heartbeat Session Timeout

## Your Task

Users report Kafka consumer groups drop membership with 'Heartbeat session timed out'. Find the Java source files in apache/kafka that (1) define the heartbeat session timeout threshold and (2) raise or log this timeout during the consumer polling loop.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the incident domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

Perfect! I've successfully analyzed the Kafka codebase and created the answer file. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I found the Java source files in Apache Kafka that handle the heartbeat session timeout mechanism:

### **Files Defining the Timeout Threshold:**
1. **CommonClientConfigs.java** - Defines the `SESSION_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG` configuration key
2. **GroupRebalanceConfig.java** - Reads and stores the `sessionTimeoutMs` value from the config
3. **Heartbeat.java** - Initializes and manages the session timeout timer

### **Files Raising/Logging the Timeout:**
1. **AbstractCoordinator.java** - Contains the `HeartbeatThread` class which:
   - Runs a background thread that continuously checks if the session timeout has expired
   - At line 1513, calls `heartbeat.sessionTimeoutExpired(now)`
   - At line 1516, calls `markCoordinatorUnknown("session timed out without receiving a heartbeat response")` when timeout expires
   - This causes the consumer to drop group membership and must rejoin

### **Key Execution Chain:**
1. `sessionTimeoutExpired()` (Heartbeat.java:119) checks if the session timer has expired
2. `HeartbeatThread` (AbstractCoordinator.java:1454+) continuously monitors this in its polling loop
3. `markCoordinatorUnknown()` (AbstractCoordinator.java:1004) is invoked when timeout expires, causing the consumer to lose group membership

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details about files, symbols, and the execution chain.

When a heartbeat response is received, receiveHeartbeat() (line 98-103) resets the session timeout timer. The heartbeat session timeout check occurs in the consumer's background heartbeat thread, implemented in AbstractCoordinator.java. The HeartbeatThread class (line 1454+) continuously runs a loop that checks heartbeat.sessionTimeoutExpired(now) at line 1513. When this check returns true, indicating that no successful heartbeat response was received within the session timeout period, the code calls markCoordinatorUnknown() at line 1516 with the message 'session timed out without receiving a heartbeat response'. This causes the consumer group coordinator to be marked as unavailable, resulting in the consumer dropping its group membership. The markCoordinatorUnknown() method (line 1004-1029) logs an info message and disconnects from the coordinator, forcing the consumer to rediscover and rejoin the group.
